<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">Recently, structural health monitoring (SHM) using radio frequency identification (RFID) tag antenna-based sensing (TABS) has received increasing attention because of its wireless, passive, and low-cost characteristics. However, a great challenge in the SHM using RFID TABS is multiple influences in the measurement. This paper presents an ultrahigh frequency RFID sensor system for corrosion detection and characterization. In this paper, a 3-D antenna sensor is designed to work on the surface of a protective coated steel sample. Sweep-frequency measurements are applied for analog identifier with principal component analysis (PCA) to overcome the multiple influences from reader-tag orientation, distance, and environment. Feature extraction and selection though PCA can get robust and sensitive defect information by projecting the test data into an orthogonal feature space. The test results demonstrate that the proposed method can be applied to detect and characterize early-stage corrosion in metals.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Structural health monitoring (SHM) and structural integrity evaluation (SIE) based on radio frequency identification (RFID) in the ultrahigh frequency (UHF) band are receiving more and more attention because of their wireless, passive, and low-cost characteristics. Integrating sensing ability in RFID tags renders the whole system capable of not only tracking, but also providing real-time cognition of aspects of objectâs status or environmental conditions <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Recently, peopleâs readiness to use RFID-based âsmart skinâ for <i>in situ</i> monitoring of the health state of large-scale infrastructure is increasing, thanks to the low cost and wide availability of RFID technology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>.</p><p>The last several decades have witnessed unprecedented prosperity in railway industry globally. Potential threats behind such a rapid expansion of railway network must be envisaged <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. The surface of the rail web (cross section connecting the rail head with the foot) and foot (base support of the rail) can be wasted by corrosion, leading to fracture and derailment <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, which will finally jeopardize the safety. Detection and characterization of corrosion is of paramount importance in railway track for safety and reliability of operation and maintenance. In contrast to conventional approaches of corrosion characterization considered as âmetal loss,â e.g., thickness changes <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, early-stage corrosion can be characterized by pitting corrosion <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, which leads to an increase in the surface roughness and reduction in the conductivity and permeability <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. Electromagnetic (EM) nondestructive testing and evaluation (NDT&amp;E) methods, such as pulsed eddy current <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, eddy current pulsed thermography (ECPT) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, and microwave waveguide <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, can be used to detect and evaluate the corrosion. The experimental results have illustrated that these EM NDT&amp;E methods are very effective to detect, evaluate, and predict the coated corrosion. However, it is difficult for these methods to permanently monitor corrosion due to the complex and bulky systems. Therefore, it is timely demanding to develop EM sensors that can be used to sense corrosion in order to undertake long-term/permanent-installed SHM and SIE. For railway monitoring, a large deployment of low-cost sensors is required owing to the large-scale structure. This makes passive RFID a good candidate among <i>in situ</i>, on-demand, and remote monitoring techniques <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>.</p><p>Low frequency (LF) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a> and high frequency (HF) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> RFID tag antenna-based sensing (TABS) were explored for detecting and characterizing corrosion under paint and insulation. Because of magnetic coupling (evanescent mode), the detection distance between LF/HF RFID tag and reader is quite short (in the range of several centimeters). UHF RFID TABS can be used to increase the monitoring distance resulting from EM coupling (radiation mode) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>. The challenges of RFID sensor system for remotely monitoring the defects of metallic objects need to address the design and development of a metal-mountable antenna for both sensing and communication, to remote access for data collection (interrogation) with good signal-to-noise ratio subjected to environment interference, and to extract features for information required <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a>. Detailed challenges and progress of RFID antenna sensors and systems can be discussed below.</p><p>Contrary to the traditional metal-mountable antenna design, TABS takes advantage of the change underneath the tagged metallic objects <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a>. The recent attempts to use UHF RFID tag antennas to monitor defects can be categorized into two main families: direct changes of antenna physical parameters and indirect changes of antenna property. For the former case, a flexible meander-line dipole was developed to monitor the strain with a submillimeter resolution <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a>. The ink-jet printing <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a> or embroidery technology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a> was applied to reduce the cost or improve the performance of strain sensors. However, the resolution and dynamic range of such a type of antennas may be influenced by each other. For the latter case, a microstrip antenna sensor was developed to monitor the growth of cracks with a sensitivity of 22 MHz/mm <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_1">[21]</a>. Moreover, a dual-resonant (TM01 and TM10 modes) microstrip antenna was proposed to detect the orientation of cracks and demonstrated that its sensivity was related to the relative permittivity and geometrical length <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_1">[22]</a>. Further information about TABS can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_1">[23]</a>.</p><p>The radio frequency (RF) signals carrying sensed information are backscattered into the wireless channel and RFID antenna sensors with the combination of sensing and communication in the system need addressing the RF channel to mitigate path loss and multipath effects <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_1">[24]</a>. In a multipath environment, backscatter RFID systems suffer from small-scale fading effects <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_1">[25]</a>, which are more severe than in classical one-way systems. The backscattered signal is subject to environmental multipath en route reader that causes both frequency and time-selective effects <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_1">[26]</a>. As a result, multiantenna techniques in RFID-based systems have come into the focus of research to overcome this drawback <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_1">[27]</a>. This technology increases the design and manufacturing costs. Since backscattered power varies depending on the distance separation between the reader and the tag, a reference tag was used for differential measurement <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_1">[28]</a>. Without <i>a priori</i> information about the tag-reader mutual position, multiple measurements can be applied for separation and reduction of multiple influence. An analog identifier (AID) was invented for this purpose <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_1">[29]</a>, which has been proved that AID is preferred among power metrics in terms of repeatability <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_1">[30]</a>. Benefited from a large variation of the tag chip impedance (nonlinearity), the influence from the environment may be mitigated by a double-power measurement technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a>.</p><p>The reader can continuously monitor the measurable parameters, e.g., forward power and backscatter power, and then features, such as resonant frequency shift (RFS), can be extracted and used to detect and characterize the defect. However, in the RFID sensor system, the contributions of the multiparameter from the defect mix with multiple influences from the environment. To this end, principal component analysis (PCA) and independent component analysis (ICA)-based pattern recognition algorithms can be used to extract the dominant variance and statistically separate the sensed signal from the interference, which have been applied in the field of NDT&amp;E to analyze data from pulsed eddy current testing for detecting metal loss <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_1">[31]</a>, cracks in multilayer structures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_1">[32]</a>, and corrosion <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_1">[33]</a>. More recently, PCA has been used to study the multiparameter effects of stress and defects in ECPT <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref34" id="context_ref_34_1">[34]</a>.</p><p>This paper is to address the challenges of detecting and characterizing corrosion in metals using RFID sensor system in terms of antenna design, system configuration, feature extraction, and corrosion characterization. A 3-D metal mountable tag antenna is proposed to optimize the tradeoff between sensing and communication. PCA is utilized to extract the defect information from multiparameter signatures of corrosion in sweep-frequency measurements. The rest of this paper is organized as follows. At first, the sensing variable and PCA will be introduced in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>, antenna sensor design will be presented. After that, test setup will be illustrated and the test results using the proposed method will be discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>. Finally, conclusions will be drawn and future work will be pointed out.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Sensing Variable and Multiparameter Analysis</h2></div><p>To develop RFID sensor system for corrosion detection and characterization, research work needs to cover tag antenna design for working on metallic surfaces with reasonable sensitivity and robust (signal) feature extraction for corrosion characterization independent of the interference. The former is left for discussion in the next <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">section III</a>, while the latter will be discussed in this section.</p><p>It is of paramount importance to mitigate multiple influences to get robust sensing information from the RFID sensor system. Several interferences, including sample surface geometry, multiple scattering due to nearby objects, and communication distance between the tag and the reader, are mixed, and thus, need to be separated.</p><p>The antenna sensor can sense the defect through the sensing variable, but the interferences change the impedance and radiation pattern of the antenna and, therefore, force the change in sensing variable as well. An analytical approach is applied to understand the measurable parameters and sensing variables. A robust sensing variable is selected.</p><p>At the same time, a mathematical processing that accounts for the effects of multiparameter signatures of corrosion is proposed. The PCA method with the help of sweep-frequency measurements is utilized to extract the dominant feature from the sensing variable. More details are explained in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2a" class="fulltext-link">Sections II-A</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2b" class="fulltext-link">II-B</a>.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. </tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of the tag antenna. </tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{align}&amp;\hspace {-2pc}P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}} [\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]=\left ({\frac {4\pi d}{\lambda _{0}}}\right )^{2}\notag \\[-1pt]&amp;\times \frac {P_{\mathrm{ th}}}{G_{R} (\theta ,\phi ) G_{T} [\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] \tau [\Psi ] \eta _{\rho }} \end{align}
</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\mathrm{ th}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-345" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-346"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-347"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-348" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-349"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-350"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-351"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-352"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-353" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-354" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">P_{\mathrm{ th}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is the minimum incident power needed to activate the tag chip (also called read sensitivity). </tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{align} \tau [\Psi ]=&amp;1-|S_{11}[\Psi ]|^{2} =1-\bigg |\frac {Z_{L} -Z_{A}^{*}[\Psi ]}{Z_{L} +Z_{A}[\Psi ]}\bigg |^{2}\notag \\=&amp;\frac {4 R_{L} R_{A} [\Psi ]}{|Z_{L} +Z_{A}[\Psi ]|^{2}}\leq 1 \end{align}

</tex-math></inline-formula> is the conjugate value of the antenna impedance. The variation of the load impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-551" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-553"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-554" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-556"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">Z_{L}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> between the values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-558" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-559"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-560"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-561" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-562"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-564" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-565" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">Z_{L1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-566" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-567"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-568"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-569" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-570"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-571"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-572" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-573" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">Z_{L2}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> (load modulation) produces two different values of the power reflection coefficients (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau _{1}[\Psi ]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-574" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-575"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-576"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-577" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Ï<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-578"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-581" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">[</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-582" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î¨</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-583" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">]</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">\tau _{1}[\Psi ]</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau _{2}[\Psi ]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-584" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-585"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-586"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-587" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Ï<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-588"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-589"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-590" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-591" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">[</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-592" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î¨</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-593" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">]</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">\tau _{2}[\Psi ]</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>).</p><p>The differential radar cross section (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \text {RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-594" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-595"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-596" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-597" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">RCS</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">\Delta \text {RCS}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>) of an RFID tag is an important parameter, which determines the power of the modulated backscattered tag signal <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref36" id="context_ref_36_2a">[36]</a>. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \text {RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-598" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-599"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-600" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-601" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">RCS</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">\Delta \text {RCS}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> can be expressed as <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_2a">[37]</a><disp-formula id="deqn5" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\begin{equation} \Delta \text {RCS}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]=\frac {\lambda _{0}^{2}}{4\pi }G_{T}^{2}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]|\tau _{1}[\Psi ]-\tau _{2} [\Psi ]|^{2} \end{equation}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-602" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-603"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-604" style="min-width: 25.108em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 25.108em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 20.964em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-1.619em 1020.96em 1.084em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -10.447em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.405em 1020.96em 5.108em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 20.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.225em 1020.96em 4.928em -999.997em); top: -3.781em; left: 50%; margin-left: -10.447em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-608"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-609"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-610" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-611" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">RCS</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-612" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">[</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-613" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î¨</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-614" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-615" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¸</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-616" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-617" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mfrac" id="MathJax-Span-621" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.123em; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-666" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">[</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-667" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î¨</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-668" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">]</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-669"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.502em; left: 0.303em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-673"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-674"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-675" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;
