right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-606"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-607" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(5)</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-25">\begin{equation} \Delta \text {RCS}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]=\frac {\lambda _{0}^{2}}{4\pi }G_{T}^{2}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]|\tau _{1}[\Psi ]-\tau _{2} [\Psi ]|^{2} \end{equation}</script>
</tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{equation} \Delta \text {RCS}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]=\frac {\lambda _{0}^{2}}{4\pi }G_{T}^{2}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )]|\tau _{1}[\Psi ]-\tau _{2} [\Psi ]|^{2} \end{equation}
</span></span></disp-formula> for both amplitude-shift-keying and phase shift-keying modulation. By means of <i>ad hoc</i> test-beds, it has been demonstrated that backscattered power exhibits a combined uncertainty ranging from 0.5 to 2 dB, with a deep dependence on the measurement instrumentation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_2a">[30]</a>.</p><p>The measurement of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \text {RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-676" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-677"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-678" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-679" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">RCS</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">\Delta \text {RCS}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> suffers from the mutual distance and orientation between the reader and tag antennas. To address this issue, an indirect measurable parameter, independent of the reader-tag mutual position and orientation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_2a">[35]</a>, can be obtained by combining the forward power <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a> and the backscattered power <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a><disp-formula id="deqn6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\begin{align} \text {AID} [\Psi ]=&amp;\frac {P_{\mathrm{ th}}}{\sqrt {P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] P_{R\leftarrow T}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] }}\notag \\=&amp;\frac {2R_{L}}{|Z_{A}[\Psi ]+Z_{L}|}. \end{align}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-27">\begin{align} \text {AID} [\Psi ]=&amp;\frac {P_{\mathrm{ th}}}{\sqrt {P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] P_{R\leftarrow T}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] }}\notag \\=&amp;\frac {2R_{L}}{|Z_{A}[\Psi ]+Z_{L}|}. \end{align}</script>
</tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{align} \text {AID} [\Psi ]=&amp;\frac {P_{\mathrm{ th}}}{\sqrt {P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] P_{R\leftarrow T}[\Psi (\theta ,\phi )] }}\notag \\=&amp;\frac {2R_{L}}{|Z_{A}[\Psi ]+Z_{L}|}. \end{align}
</span></span></disp-formula> In <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is the corresponding backscattered power in the tagâs absorbing state, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is the turn ON power. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> can be gathered, in principle, by the differential backscattered powers in the absorbing and reflecting states <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_2a">[17]</a>, or received signal strength indicator.</p><p>Comparing with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \text {RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">\Delta \text {RCS}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, AID has a robust feature due to the ratio of power that is only related to impedance rather than antenna gain <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2a">[15]</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Multiparameter Analysis</h3><p>The sensing mechanism of the UHF RFID TABS is similar to the pulsed eddy current technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2b">[8]</a>, which uses alternating magnetic (evanescent) field to generate eddy current and then interacts with the sample. The surface roughness, thickness, conductivity, and permeability of steel and corroded area contribute to the variation of the tag antennaâs impedance.</p><p>To simplify the analysis, the observation matrix is assumed to be a mixture of several sources, additive scatter, and noise with mixing weight, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m_{i} (i=1,2,3,4)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">m_{i} (i=1,2,3,4)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. The mathematical definition of the mixing model can be described as <disp-formula id="deqn7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\begin{equation} Y=\sum _{i=1}^{N_{S}}m_{i}X_{i}+S+N \end{equation}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-35">\begin{equation} Y=\sum _{i=1}^{N_{S}}m_{i}X_{i}+S+N \end{equation}</script>
</tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{equation} Y=\sum _{i=1}^{N_{S}}m_{i}X_{i}+S+N \end{equation}
</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{S}=4</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">N_{S}=4</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> denotes the number of sources. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">X_{1,2,3,4}(f)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">X_{1,2,3,4}(f)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> refers to the defect variable <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\Psi )</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">(\Psi )</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, including thickness, surface roughness, conductivity, and permeability of corrosion layer and steel. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S(f)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">S(f)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> refers to the scatter caused by nearby objects and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N(f)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">N(f)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> represents noise, e.g., phase noise of the reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_2b">[38]</a>. The first term of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> is bearing the multiparameter defect information. The second term, nearby objects in the reader or tag, leads to an uncertainty in the measurement of forward and backscattered powers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref39" id="context_ref_39_2b">[39]</a>.</p><p>PCA is utilized to extract the dominant feature. The details of data processing method used in this paper are depicted in the following steps <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_2b">[40]</a>:
</p><ol><li><p>Organize the data set as an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N \times M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">N \times M</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> matrix, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">N</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is the number of corrosion samples used and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">M</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is the number of the frequency points of the sweep-frequency measurement.</p></li><li><p>Normalize the data to have zero mean and unity variance.</p></li><li><p>Calculate the eigenvectorsâeigenvalues of the covariance matrix by singular value decomposition.</p></li><li><p>Select the first and second eigenvectors corresponding to the first and second largest eigenvalues as the first principal component (PC1) and second principal component (PC2).</p></li><li><p>Transform the original data onto the selected PCs and obtain the corresponding projection coefficients (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{s}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">\Omega _{s}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>).</p></li></ol><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">\Omega _{2}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> are selected as the new features, which represent the projections of AIDs onto the PC1 and PC2, respectively.<p></p><p>By projecting the measurement quantity into an orthogonal space spanned by the eigenvectors of the covariance matrix corresponding to the maximum variability within the data, PCA is used to extract the dominant variance from multiparameter signatures of the defect, to mitigate multiple effects from nearby objects, and to reduce the noise.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Antenna Sensor Design</h2></div><p>In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, we analyzed a robust sensing variable and feature extraction method. To design a specific antenna with a reasonable sensitivity and communication distance, the physical, chemical, and electrical properties of the corrosion sample need to be taken into consideration. With the help of simulation, this section presents the EM modeling of corrosion stages, the design rule of a prototype antenna sensor, and the optimization procedure to balance the tradeoff between sensing and communication.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Sample Preparation</h3><p>Corrosion in steel is a general term for a series of iron oxides (hematite <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\alpha </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">\alpha </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, magnetite Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>, and maghemite <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\gamma </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">\gamma </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>) and hydroxides [ferrous hydroxide Fe(OH), ferric hydroxide Fe(OH)3, and goethite <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\alpha </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">\alpha </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>-FeOOH], and over time only the proportions of the corrosion constituents change, there is little effect on the composition <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3a">[8]</a>.</p><p>According to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref41" id="context_ref_41_3a">[41]</a>, the electrical conductivity and relative permeability of steel are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">4.68 \times 10^{6}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">4.68 \times 10^{6}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> S/m and 60, while the electrical conductivity and relative permeability of corrosion are about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">0.75\times 10^{6}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">0.75\times 10^{6}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> S/m and 4, respectively. Therefore, the skin depth is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">0.9~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">0.9~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> in steel and approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">9.2~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">9.2~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> in corroded area at 1 GHz. The effect of the loss from eddy current induced by surface roughness can be neglected, if their dimensions are not comparable, on the average, to the skin depth <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref42" id="context_ref_42_3a">[42]</a>. Because of the increase in the surface roughness, the conductivity of the corroded area will decrease with the corrosion progression.</p><p>The samples (mild steel S275) used in this paper, with length <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">\times </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\times </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> height of 300 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times150</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\times150</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">\times3</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm, are provided by International Paint [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>], the center part (corroded area with a size of 30 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times30</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">\times30</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm) of which was exposed to a marine atmosphere for a certain time (0, 1, 3, 6, 10, and 12 months), and then, covered using a nonconductive paint in a thickness of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim 100~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\sim 100~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. For reference convenience, these six-stage samples are, respectively, represented as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">M0</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">M1</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">M3</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M6</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">M6</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">M10</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M12</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">M12</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. The corrosion samples can be divided into two categories <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref43" id="context_ref_43_3a">[43]</a>: early stage (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">M0</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">M1</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">M3</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M6</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">M6</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>) and later stage (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">M10</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M12</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">M12</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang1ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang1ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang1ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang1ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>(a) Corrosion samples in six different stages and (b) simplified model.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>To facilitate early detection and characterization of corrosion, this paper focuses on the early-stage ones, where pitting corrosion is dominant. At this stage, the corrosion layer thickness (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">t)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> increases as corrosion progresses <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3a">[8]</a>. This parameter becomes an interesting signature to be measured. For simplicity, the covering layer can be treated as a dry-air film and the corrosion sample is, therefore, modeled as a multilayered structure, which is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Antenna Design for Sensing and Communication</h3><p>To achieve an optimal tradeoff between sensing and communication is a major consideration in the design of an antenna sensor. The proximity coupling between the antenna and the tagged object can be utilized for sensing purpose when disturbance underneath the antenna sensor occurs at a presence of corrosion. The high-quality-factor antenna offers a better sensitivity for sensing, but can be costly to implement and difficult to attach to the surface of a flat metallic structure <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref44" id="context_ref_44_3b">[44]</a>. Owing to the edge effect <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref45" id="context_ref_45_3b">[45]</a>, the antenna size needs to be reduced down to corrosion patch to maximize the sensitivity. For these reasons, the antenna should be electrically small in order to be more sensitive. In addition, the cost consideration in manufacturing requires a simple antenna structure as well as use of lossy substrate materials. This will substantially reduce the communication distance. In complementary, a larger height profile (aspect ratio) is required to enhance the reading performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref46" id="context_ref_46_3b">[46]</a>. This may also lead to a quasi-omnidirectional radiation pattern above tagged object, allowing tag to be easily identified.</p><p>A 3-D cage antenna is proposed to facilitate the size reduction and to be conjugately matched with a capacitive load, i.e., tag chip. The antenna is prototyped for conjugate impedance matching to the passive tag chip of IMPINJ MONZA 4QT in the single-port connection, the input impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(Z_{L})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">(Z_{L})</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and nominal read sensitivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{\mathrm{ th}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">(P_{\mathrm{ th}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>) of which are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">11-j143~\Omega </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">11-j143~\Omega </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and â17.4 dBm at 915 MHz, respectively. The equivalent input impedance of this chip can be treated as a 1.65-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\text{k}\Omega </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">\text{k}\Omega </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> resistor connected in parallel with a 1.21-pF capacitor <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref47" id="context_ref_47_3b">[47]</a>. An FR4 material, with a loss tangent of 0.02 and a relative permittivity of 4.4, is used in this design. The proposed antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a>, the substrate of which consists of ten layers of FR4 lamination, with a standard thickness of 1.6 mm for each layer. The total size of the antenna is 20 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times20</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">\times20</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\times16</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">\times16</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm. The reason for the selection of the height profile (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">h)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> will be further discussed from sensing point of view in the next part.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang2abc-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang2abc-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang2abc-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang2abc-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>(a) Proposed 3-D metal mountable UHF RFID tag antenna. (b) Simulated current distribution. (c) Equivalent circuit, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{m} = 0.57</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">C_{m} = 0.57</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> pF, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\mathrm {ca1}} = 6.81</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">L_{\mathrm {ca1}} = 6.81</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> nH, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{ca1} = 1.08~\Omega </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">R_{ca1} = 1.08~\Omega </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\mathrm {ca2}} = 6.81</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">L_{\mathrm {ca2}} = 6.81</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> nH, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\mathrm {ca2}} = 1.08~\Omega </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">R_{\mathrm {ca2}} = 1.08~\Omega </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\mathrm {a2c}} = 14.45</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">C_{\mathrm {a2c}} = 14.45</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> pF, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{l2r} = 1.67</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">L_{l2r} = 1.67</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> nH, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{a2m} = 15.70</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">C_{a2m} = 15.70</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> pF at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w} = 5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">{w} = 5</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t = 40~\mu </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">t = 40~\mu </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> m.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>To enable the sensing ability for such a tag antenna, an open-ended slot is first etched on the sensing patch, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a>. Consequently, an enhancement in the current distribution can be formed near the slot [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>]. Second, we deploy the antenna in the edge of corroded area; hence, the corrosion and steel will, respectively, affect the left and right parts of the sensing patch, and thus, generates an uneven current distribution in this patch. Since the antenna is directly mounted on the corrosion sample, the distance of the antenna to the corroded area is fixed. Using such a configuration, we can measure the thickness difference between the corrosion layer and the base material (steel).</p><p>The lumped circuit analogy is given out in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a> to gain a physical insight into the operation of the proposed antenna sensor and find the variation of the sensing variable as corrosion progresses. We can generate an equivalent circuit model for the proposed antenna sensor by starting from the cage structure, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">C_{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> represents the feeding gap, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\mathrm {cax}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">L_{\mathrm {cax}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\mathrm {cax}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">R_{\mathrm {cax}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">x = 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">x = 1</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, 2) represent the inductance and resistance (including loss) of the cage structure. The displacement and longitudinal current in the open-ended slot can be, respectively, modeled by two parallel capacitors and one inductor in series connected in between. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{a2c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">C_{a2c}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is to account for the capacitive coupling of the antenna to the corroded area, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{a2m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">C_{a2m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is to account for the capacitive coupling between the antenna and the base material (steel), and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{l2r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">L_{l2r}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is to account for the strip connected the left and right parts of the sensing patch, which is influenced by the slot with (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">{w})</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. The parameter of interest, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">t</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, can be quantified by the sensing component of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{a2m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">C_{a2m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. Consequently, it varies along with corrosion progression, which will influence the impedance matching of the antenna, and thus, can be indirectly measured via the sensing variable, i.e., AID.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Forward Problem Analysis for Optimization</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the simulated reflection coefficients (S11) and AIDs of the proposed antenna. The simulated 3-dB impedance bandwidth of the proposed antenna is larger than 50 MHz. It is straightforward that the resonant frequency of the proposed antenna drops as an increase of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">h</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> owing to the increase of the inductance [<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\mathrm {cax}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">L_{\mathrm {cax}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a>]. Besides, because of an increase in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{l2r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">L_{l2r}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, the resonant frequency of the antenna will slightly decrease as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> increases. 
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang3ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang3ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang3ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang3ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Simulated (a) reflection coefficients (S11) and (b) AIDs in the variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t = 40~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">t = 40~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The simulated radiation pattern and realized gain, which have taken into consideration the impedance mismatch loss between the antenna and the tag chip <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref48" id="context_ref_48_3c">[48]</a>, are depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a) and (b)</a>, respectively. The nondirectional radiation pattern, resulting from the radiation in both horizontal and vertical radiating patches, makes the tag be easily identified in a wide range of spatial angles in both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">E</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> (<i>yz</i>) and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-107">H </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>(<i>xz</i>) planes [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a)</a>]. From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(b)</a>, we see that the proposed antenna can reach its peak realized gain of 0.6 dBi at 934 MHz. The reason for the selection of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> will be discussed later in this section. Nevertheless, we can find that the peak realized gain slightly decreases with the increase of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-109">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. 
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang4ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang4ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang4ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang4ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>(a) Simulated radiation pattern at 915 MHz when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w} = 5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">{w} = 5</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t = 40~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">t = 40~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) Simulated realized gain versus frequency in the variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t = 40~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">t = 40~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(a)</a> shows the simulated input impedances of the proposed antenna sensor in the variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">t</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. It can be observed that a substantial change in the resistance occurs when corrosion happens. This is directly caused by a significant reduction in the resistance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\mathrm {ca1}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">R_{\mathrm {ca1}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">1.30~\Omega </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">1.30~\Omega </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> at the healthy state and to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">1.08~\Omega </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">1.08~\Omega </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> at the corrosion states (and maintained almost at different corrosion stages), which can be attributed to a reduction of eddy current loss at a presence of corrosion. 
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang5ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang5ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang5ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang5ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>(a) Simulated input impedances of the proposed antenna sensor versus frequency in the variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">t</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}= 5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">{w}= 5</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm. (b) Simulated and modeled AIDs versus frequency in the variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">t</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w} = 5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">{w} = 5</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm. Solid line: simulated results. Dashed line: modeled ones.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(b)</a> shows a comparison of the simulated results of AIDs using full wave simulation with the results using an equivalent circuit model. Good agreement can be found, which demonstrates that the sensing principle can be reasonably reconstructed in terms of a capacitive sensing component. The increase in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">t</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> leads to an increase in the displacement current (due to the cavity theory), thus rendering an increase in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{a2m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-123">C_{a2m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. This drops the resonant frequency as corrosion progresses.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(a)</a> shows a feature of single frequency (SF) directly extracted from AID. It can be found that the corrosion layer thickness produces a monotonic shift in AID in the frequency away from resonance. Therefore, SF (or RFS) can be used to act as a feature to <i>detect</i> and <i>characterize</i> the corrosion in metals. To compare the sensitivity of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-124">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and SF, a minâmax normalization method is used in its feasible region to conduct a dimensionless analysis, and the results are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(b)</a>. We see that the sensitivity of SF increases with the increase of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and reaches the peak value when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w} = 4</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">{w} = 4</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm. However, it is not maximized near the resonant frequency (e.g., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-127">f_{0})</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, which complicates the selection of frequency points, particularly in autonomous scenarios, and also leads to a tradeoff between sensing (sensitivity) and communication (distance). 
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang6ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang6ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang6ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang6ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>(a) Simulated AIDs versus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-128">t</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> in the variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{w}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-129-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-129">{w}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{-1} = 860</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-130-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-130">f_{-1} = 860</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> MHz, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0} = 915</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-131-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-131">f_{0} = 915</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> MHz, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{+1} = 960</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-132-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-132">f_{+1} = 960</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> MHz. (b) Sensitivities of different features, where PCA<sub>0</sub> and PCA<sub>3</sub> represent the feature of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively, extracted from the frequency band of 902â928 and 860â960 MHz when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h = 16.0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-134">h = 16.0</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm, while PCA<sub>1</sub> and PCA<sub>2</sub> represent the feature of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-135">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> extracted from the frequency band of 902â928 MHz when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-136">h</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is 16.5 and 17 mm, respectively.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Similarly, by comparing PCA<sub>0</sub>, PCA<sub>1</sub>, and PCA<sub>2</sub>, we can find that the sensitivity of the PCA method is related to the resonant frequency (or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-137">h)</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. In contrary to the feature of SF, the PCA method uses the shape information; hence its sensitivity can be maximized even a small bandwidth is available, e.g., 902â928 MHz in this paper. Therefore, to achieve an optimal tradeoff between sensing and communication, the proposed antenna is tuned to resonate at 934 MHz at the healthy state, a little higher than the upper bound of the measurable frequency region. Meanwhile, a slot width of 5 mm is selected for the experimental study to ease the deployment of the tag. This is also attributed to the reason where the corrosion that happens is unknown in <i>a priori</i> for practical applications.</p><p>By properly choosing the antenna size and topology (radiation mode), designing the matching performance, and deploying the antenna, an acceptable tradeoff between sensing (sensitivity) and communication (distance) based on UHF RFID TABS can be achieved. Based on the design, experimental studies and validation of corrosion detection and characterization are examined in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">section IV</a>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Measurements and Discussion</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Experimental Setup</h3><p>The forward and backscattered powers of the tag were measured using a ThingMagic Mercury xPRESS platform. The test setup and software flowchart of the RFID sensor system are depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. The distance between the reader and tag antennas was fixed to 1 m. The reader antenna is circularly polarized with a 6-dBi gain when the radiated power was decreased from 30 dBm in a step of 0.5 dB to find the threshold power to activate the tag <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-138">(P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}})</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and corresponding backscattered power (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>), hence yielding a maximum 4-W effective isotropic radiated power. Owing to the firmware limitation, the measurement was only carried out under the operating frequency of 902â928 MHz and the reader was set to increase 1 MHz per step. The test was repeated four times for each sample for robustness.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang7ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang7ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang7ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang7ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>(a) Hardware measurement setup. (b) Software flowchart of the RFID sensor system.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Results and Discussion</h3><p>In order to evaluate the performance of the proposed method, a test was carried out in a typical office in the presence of tables, boxes, metallic cabinets, and other sources of clutter <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref49" id="context_ref_49_4b">[49]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a> shows the four times measurements of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency in the variation of samples. Comparing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-142">P_{\mathrm{ in}}^{\mathrm{ to}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-143-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-143">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, we can find a significant improvement in the sensitivity for the forward power to activate tag, which can be attributed to the higher power resolution of the transmitter and power-starved property in the forward link <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref50" id="context_ref_50_4b">[50]</a> while a major limitation for the measurement of backscattered power is the resolution of analog-to-digital converter (ADC) in the receiver. Because of the lossy FR4 substrate and the limited measurement bandwidth, it is not easy to find the resonant frequency. 
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang8ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang8ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang8ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang8ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Measured (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{in}^{to}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-144-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-144">P_{in}^{to}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\leftarrow T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-145-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-145">P_{R\leftarrow T}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and (b) AIDs versus frequency in the variation of corrosion progression.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(a)</a> shows the projection coefficients of the AIDs [shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a>] onto the PC1 and PC2, reflecting major corrosion progression, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-147">\Omega _{2}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> represents the dominant variance (more than 97%) of corrosion signatures, it is then selected as a feature for corrosion characterization. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(b)</a> illustrates the features extracted from PCA method and SF. We can find that the sensing variable of AID through both of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-149">f_{0}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-150">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> can identify the corrosion progression in the early stage. However, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-151-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-151">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> demonstrates a better robustness. The corroded area becomes loose and flakes off as it expands, and this shows that later-stage corrosion will spread rather than increase in thickness <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_4b">[8]</a>. That is, metal loss becomes dominant in the later stage and this explains why the abnormality incurs in the 10 and 12 months corrosion. The results are in line with the previous studies using vector network analyzer and waveguides <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_4b">[13]</a>. In addition, measured with laser profilometry, the average value of corrosion layer thickness for one, three, and six months exposed corrosion samples were about 43, 77, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">108~\mu \text{m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-152-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-152">108~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref51" id="context_ref_51_4b">[51]</a>. Therefore, the proposed method of RFID sensor system using AID and PCA shows good agreement with the previous measurements on the dedicated samples. 
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang9ab-2596898-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang9ab-2596898-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang9ab-2596898_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8/7582347/7529044/zhang9ab-2596898_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>(a) Distributions of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-153-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-153">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-154-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-154">\Omega _{2}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> for the corrosion samples. (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-155-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-155">f_{0}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-156-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-156">\Omega _{1}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> versus corrosion progression. Dashed line: extracted feature using SF. Solid line: extracted feature using PCA method.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7529044/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Data supporting this publication is openly available under an âOpen Data Commons Open Database Licenseâ <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref52" id="context_ref_52_4b">[52]</a>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A 3-D UHF RFID tag antenna has been designed to sense the corrosion in metals. PCA has been used to extract sensing information by a sweep-frequency measurement of AID, which relieves the challenge in the antenna design, while enhances the sensitivity and robustness. The developed RFID sensor system can successfully detect and characterize the corrosion stages and remotely measure the corrosionâs information via a reader and a tag in a stand-off distance. It inherits the advantage of pulsed eddy current for NDT&amp;E and demonstrates a cost-effective way to implement distributed monitoring. This approach has potential to bridge the gaps of NDT&amp;E and SHM for industry application.</p><p>However, there are some limitations. The first is that one dedicated antenna is investigated for a set of dedicated samples. The second is that the RFID grid needs to be studied for distributed monitoring. Future work will focus on how to solve these limitations and improve the RFID sensor system, which includes the design and development of more antennas for different defects and samples. Different measurement strategies from readers will be further investigated as well.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENTS</h3><p>The authors would like to thank the International Paint Ltd., Tyne and Wear, U.K., for supplying the corrosion samples, to the EPSRC for the funding of the Novel Sensing Networks for Intelligent Monitoring (NEWTON) project (EP/J012343/1), and K. Blacktop from Network Rail for the helpful discussion about the application of RFID sensor system along railway tracks.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

However, a great challenge in the SHM using RFID TABS is multiple influences in the measurement. This paper presents an ultrahigh frequency RFID sensor system for corrosion detection and characterization. In this paper, a 3-D antenna sensor is designed to work on the surface of a protective coated steel sample. Sweep-frequency measurements are applied for analog identifier with principal component analysis (PCA) to overcome the multiple influences from reader-tag orientation, distance, and environment. Feature extraction and selection though PCA can get robust and sensitive defect information by projecting the test data into an orthogonal feature space.
